EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
[COMPANY] (Pinchin) was retained by [COMPANY] on behalf of [COMPANY] (Client) to conduct a Phase I Environmental Site Assessment ([COMPANY]) of the property located at
1500 Fisher Street, [LOCATION], Ontario (hereafter referred to as the Site) (Morguard Property No.
12254p01).
The Site is developed with a single-storey enclosed commercial shopping centre style building, complete
with a partial second-storey located within the central and east portions of the building (Site Building),
commonly referred to as the ‘Northgate Shopping Centre’. In addition, a five-level, above grade parking
garage is located to the southwest portion of [COMPANY].
[PERSON] was advised by the [CITY] that the purpose of the Phase I [COMPANY] was to assess potential issues of
environmental concern for due diligence purposes and for potential future real estate transactions (i.e.,
financing or dispositions) as required to meet Morguard’s business needs.
The Phase I [COMPANY] was completed in general accordance with [COMPANY] ([COMPANY])
document entitled “Phase I Environmental Site Assessment, CSA Standard Z768-01” dated November
2001 (reaffirmed 2022), including a review of readily-available historical records, a review of readily-
accessible regulatory records, a Site reconnaissance, interviews, an evaluation of information and
reporting, subject to the limitations outlined in Section 8.0 of this report.
Based on the results of the Phase I [COMPANY] completed by [PERSON], nothing was identified that is likely to
result in potential subsurface impacts at the Site. As such, no subsurface investigation work (Phase II
ESA) is recommended at this time.
To the best of [PERSON]’s knowledge, activities at the Site appear to generally be conducted using best
practices for handling of chemicals, hazardous wastes, air emissions, and/or potentially hazardous
building materials (e.g., asbestos, lead, etc.), and no obvious non-conformances with applicable
environmental regulations were identified. Based on a review of the 2019 Pinchin Exemption Report, it
was determined that the existing heating and emergency generator meet the O.Reg.524 Section 9
exemption criteria. A compliance audit was not completed by [PERSON] as part of this assessment, and as
such this statement is limited to [PERSON]’s observations during the Site reconnaissance, and information
available during the Site reconnaissance, provided by [COMPANY], or obtained from
referenced regulatory sources within the Phase I ESA. Pinchin notes that according to a 2023
Environmental Compliance Audit completed at the Site by another consultant, no compliance issues
requiring immediate action were identified at the Site.
[COMPANY] is subject to the same standard limitations as contained in the report and must be
read in conjunction with the entire report.

1.0 INTRODUCTION
1.1 [COMPANY] (Pinchin) was retained by [COMPANY] on behalf of [COMPANY] Morguard ITF [COMPANY] (Client) to conduct a Phase I Environmental Site
Assessment ([COMPANY]) of the property located at 1500 Fisher Street, [LOCATION], Ontario (hereafter referred to
as the Site) (Morguard Property No. 12254p01).
The Site is developed with a single-storey enclosed commercial shopping centre style building, complete
with a partial second-storey located within the central and east portions of the building (Site Building),
commonly referred to as the ‘Northgate Shopping Centre’. In addition, a five-level, above grade parking
garage is located to the southwest portion of [COMPANY].
[PERSON] was advised by the [CITY] that the purpose of the Phase I [COMPANY] was to assess potential issues of
environmental concern for due diligence purposes and for potential future real estate transactions (i.e.,
financing or dispositions) as required to meet Morguard’s business needs.
1.2 Scope of Work
The Phase I [COMPANY] was completed in general accordance with [COMPANY] ([COMPANY])
document entitled “Phase I Environmental Site Assessment, CSA Standard Z768-01” dated November
2001 (reaffirmed 2022), including a review of readily-available historical records, a review of readily-
accessible regulatory records, a Site reconnaissance, interviews, an evaluation of information and
reporting, subject to the limitations outlined in Section 8.0 of this report.
The Phase I [COMPANY] was completed in accordance with [COMPANY] between [COMPANY] and the [CITY], dated November 2011.
Pinchin conducted a Site reconnaissance on April 26, 2024, and was accompanied by the [COMPANY]
Manager for the Site since approximately 2022, who is hereafter referred to as the Site Representative.
In addition, [PERSON] was provided numerous previous reports pertaining to the Site. Only the necessary
documents and reports were to be reviewed in detail as considered appropriate by the [PERSON] (as noted
in the Request for Proposal). However, the following relevant documents were provided and reviewed
(where applicable) by [PERSON] as part of the Phase I ESA:

of the Site. The Site is situated in an area that predominantly consists of vacant/undeveloped, residential,
commercial, parkland and light industrial land uses. Figure 2 illustrates the Site and surrounding area.

hydraulically-operated passenger elevators and one-hydraulically-operated freight elevator service the
Site Building.

transects the west portion of the Site in a north-south direction. Main ingress/egress to [COMPANY] is
located along the central and north portions of [COMPANY] along west exterior elevation.
Site maintenance activities involve painting, replacement of light fixtures, minor plumbing and electrical
work on an as-needed basis.

that this spill is unlikely to result in potential subsurface impacts at the Site.

5.5 Polychlorinated Biphenyls
The use of polychlorinated biphenyls (PCBs) in electrical equipment such as transformers, fluorescent
lamp ballasts, and capacitors was common until Canada banned its use in 1980. The Federal PCB
Regulations, SOR/2008-273, regulate the manufacture, import, export, sale, use and processing of PCBs.
These regulations required the decommissioning of equipment containing high levels of PCBs (>500 parts
per million [ppm]) in 2009. Additionally, the regulations require decommissioning of light ballasts, pole top
transformers, capacitors and electrical equipment containing greater than 50 milligrams per kilogram
PCBs by December 31, 2025. Cables, pipelines and equipment associated with natural gas, petroleum
and petroleum products, and fusion sealed capacitors for use in communication equipment and electrical
control equipment are exempt from the decommissioning requirement.
Given the year of construction of the Site Building (i.e., approximately 1961)(i.e., approximately 1961 and
1980), the following table outlines the potentially [COMPANY]-containing equipment/material observed on-Site

5.6 [COMPANY] materials (ACMs) are commonly found in building construction materials (particularly
in older buildings). Asbestos use in building products declined in use starting in the 1970s, with the
majority of products being phased out by circa 1990. Asbestos use in Canada was formally banned in
December 2018.
Friable asbestos (friable is defined as a material that can be crumbled, powdered or pulverized by hand
pressure) was widely used in sprayed fireproofing until 1973, and in decorative or finishing plasters, and
thermal systems insulation until the early 1980s. Non-friable or manufactured asbestos products were
widely used in building construction including in vinyl floor tiles, sheet flooring, ceiling tiles, pipe gaskets,
roofing materials, asbestos cement boards, and numerous other products until circa 1990. A limited
number of non-friable asbestos products remained in use until the end of 2018; examples include friction
materials, gaskets, cement pipes, sealants, adhesives and caulking.
Given the years of construction of the original portions of [COMPANY] (i.e., approximately 1961, 1980
and 1990), it is considered that there is a potential for ACMs to be present within the original portions of
the Site Building. Given the years of construction of the Site Buildings’ additions (i.e., 2001 and 2015), it is
considered that there is a low potential for ACMs to be present within the Site Buildings additions.
[PERSON] did not conduct an asbestos survey, nor was any destructive or intrusive sampling or inspection
conducted; however, multiple asbestos surveys have been completed at the Site by [COMPANY], ECOH, [CITY],
S2S, [COMPANY] and [PERSON] throughout the Site Building dating back to as early as 2006. Based on a review
of reports provided by the Client, ACMs (i.e., black window caulking, vinyl floor tiles, lay-in ceiling tiles,
parging cement on fittings, vinyl sheet flooring, mastic, duct connector and tar) and presumed ACMs (i.e.,
Transite® piping, lay-in ceiling tiles, bells and spigot joints and parging cement on fittings) are located at
the Site.

1500 Fisher Street, [LOCATION], Ontario Pinchin File: 337479.004
Morguard ITF [COMPANY] c/o [COMPANY] FINAL
ACMs were noted to be in good condition at the time of [COMPANY] reconnaissance. Abatement

5.7 Lead-Containing Paints
Lead was commonly used as an additive in paints with no restricted level up until the mid-1970s. This
included architectural paints used on interior and exterior surfaces, primers and coatings for anti-corrosive
purposes, consumer paints, and paint on furniture and other household items.
Beginning in 1976, the federal government limited the amount of lead in consumer paints to 5,000 ppm
and steadily reduced the lead content, primarily in the interest of public safety. In 2005, the limit was
reduced to 600 ppm and in 2010, the limit was further reduced to 90 ppm, however, there is no restriction
on lead in paints used for anti-corrosion purposes (e.g., steel primers and exterior coatings) and road and
line markings. In June 2016, these exemptions were removed and as of this date, any paint sold should
not contain more than 90 ppm, even if sold for anti-corrosion purposes.
[PERSON] did not conduct an assessment of lead in painted surfaces as part of this Phase I [COMPANY]; however,
designated substance surveys have been completed for [COMPANY]. Based on a review of former
[COMPANY] completed for the Site. it was noted that all painted surfaces with any
detectable presence of lead were considered to be lead-containing. Further, it was noted that lead-
containing batteries are present within the exit signs and suspected lead-containing solder is present on
domestic water pipes. During Pinchin’s Site reconnaissance, painted surfaces (where observed) were in
good condition (i.e., no peeling or flaking).

5.9 Radon
Radon is a naturally occurring radioactive gas formed by the breakdown of uranium in soil, rocks and
even groundwater. [COMPANY] is invisible, odourless and colourless and as such, cannot be detected by
humans. Radon escapes from the ground and mixes with outdoor air forming concentrations that are too
low to be of concern; however, if radon enters a building the concentrations can increase to higher levels.
[COMPANY] has developed guidelines for acceptable levels of radon in dwellings and public buildings
and has indicated that radon levels should not exceed 200 Becquerel per [PERSON] (Bq/m3). Testing for
radon in [COMPANY] was beyond the scope of this Phase I ESA. However, the 2018 Pinchin Radon
Report indicated that based on the levels of radon measured within the Site Building, no further action
was required.
5.10 Mould or [COMPANY]
The presence of mould or other microbiological contamination in buildings has become a concern to
building tenants and owners due to potential health effects on occupants and users. [COMPANY]
of [COMPANY] have recently issued guidelines on enforced regulations to protect the health of construction
workers who are exposed to mould in the course of building renovation. The presence of water leaks or
high humidity can cause the growth or amplification of mould within building environments.

managed by the Site Representative.

with the [COMPANY] or in Opta’s possession at the time of Report delivery to the purchaser. The Documents are current
as of the date(s) indicated on them. Interpretation of the Documents, if any, is by inference based upon the information

Limitations and Notices:
General:
TSSA, as a safety regulator, uses inspection resources to address the greatest harm posed to the public.
Thus, inspection only follows-up on safety orders it issues based on the degree of risk posed by the non-
compliance identified in the order(s). All high-risk orders will result in a follow-up inspection by TSSA until
the non-compliance is resolved. TSSA no longer follows-up on low or medium risk orders referred to as
safety tasks, therefore, TSSA can no longer provide you with a report indicating the safety tasks (low and
medium-risk orders) have been resolved. This information should be obtained from the device/facility
owner or their contractor. One can also engage a third-party contractor to confirm device/facility
compliance.
[COMPANY], ([COMPANY]), can only provide existing records for a specific location, facility,
or device. If an inspection or any other type of record does not exist, [COMPANY] cannot instruct TSSA to do
work, such as an inspection, to create a record. TSSA, as an outcome-based regulator, deploys all of its
resources, including, inspections to address the greatest harm posed to the public; and as such, cannot
deploy resources to create records to satisfy an inquiry.
Please Note: While the [COMPANY] provides existing records for a specific location, facility, or device; it does not
interpret or provide further explanations of the content contained in the document.
[COMPANY] be advised, if the new owner has acquired a property that contains TSSA regulated devices, i.e.
elevators, boilers and pressure vessels, they would be required to complete a change of ownership to
obtain new licences. Visit our website at www.tssa.org under [COMPANY] section for the
Change of Ownership process or contact our [COMPANY] department at [PHONE]
TSSA Fuels Safety:
If you have environmental concerns regarding this property, you should consider hiring an environmental
consultant to conduct an environmental assessment of the property in question.
• Sites that have not been licensed since 1987 may not be in TSSA records.
[PERSON] advised, TSSA Fuels Safety Division did not register:
• private fuel underground/ aboveground storage tanks prior to January of 1990; and
• furnace oil tanks prior to May 1, 2002.
• If records being released to you relate to private fuel outlets (“PFOs”) or fuel oil furnace tanks, please
note the following:
• PFOs are defined in [PERSON]. 217/01 (Liquid [PERSON]), where “private outlet” means “any premise,
other than a retail outlet, where gasoline or an associated product is put into the fuel tanks of
motor vehicles or floating motorized watercraft or into portable containers”. After 2001, PFOs
were no longer required to be licenced in Ontario. Thus, TSSA’s records and information
regarding PFOs is dated and unverified.
• Underground furnace fuel oil tanks were required to be registered with TSSA commencing in
2001. These underground tanks are registered; however, [COMPANY] does not inspect or verify the
Page 2 of 4
registered tank information. It is incumbent on the fuel distributor to ensure that the tanks are
registered. Above ground fuel oil furnace tanks do not require TSSA registration.
[COMPANY] be advised that while the [COMPANY] releases information relating to PFOs or fuel oil furnace
tanks pursuant to [COMPANY], the TSSA cautions against reliance on
this information.
• In particular, because PFOs do not require a license and there is no requirement to submit any
documentation to TSSA for review or approval, [COMPANY] has limited information on these facilities.
The TSSA cautions that any information provided may be inaccurate, incomplete, or out of date.
[COMPANY] does not register
• private waste oil tanks in apartments, office buildings, residences etc.; and
• aboveground gas or diesel tanks.
[COMPANY] and associated regulations do not require the registration of
private fuel outlets, nor does it require that any documentation on these facilities be submitted to or
reviewed or approved by [COMPANY]. As a result, [COMPANY] has limited information on these facilities. TSSA
cautions that any information provided may be inaccurate, incomplete or out of date.

• The Ontario Amusement Devices Regulation (O. Reg. 221/01) was adopted in 2001. Since that time,

retention policy). However, for rides that existed prior to the adoption of the [COMPANY], which were

[COMPANY] be advised that without the express written consent of the owner, the [COMPANY] does not release
any information with respect to federal elevators or federal elevating equipment. The TSSA is a
provincial regulator for the province of Ontario and federal elevators do not fall within the scope of
[COMPANY]’s provincial mandate and [COMPANY] and associated Regulations.
Further, [COMPANY] only applies to information collected, used, or disclosed
by the TSSA in the course of [COMPANY]’s administration of the Act. Therefore, information with respect to
federal elevators or federal elevator equipment is outside of the administration of the Act, and outside
of the scope of [COMPANY].

TSSA Boilers and Pressure Vessels (BPVs) Program Notice:
• Be advised, [COMPANY] does not typically periodically inspect BPVs. These inspections are usually
performed by insurance companies.
• **Inspection reports may not be submitted to TSSA by insurance companies; therefore, while TSSA
may have some evidence of a BPV at a location on file, there may be no inspection records pertaining
to BPVs located at the address provided.
• As of July 1, 2018, BPVs in Ontario may not be operated unless the Director has issued a current
certificate of inspection (COI) to the owner or operator. A COI will be issued to the owner or operator
of the BPV by TSSA after [COMPANY] has received a Record of Inspection (ROI) from the insurer/third-party
inspector, the associated fees have been paid and the BPV has passed a periodic inspection.
[COMPANY] note that if the BPV in question is insured, the insurance company may have additional
inspection records. Please contact the insurer directly should you wish to obtain further information.

[COMPANY]: Provincial Arr-AAAGGR-bRb
[COMPANY] maintains a database of abandoned pits and quarries. Please note that the database is only referenced by lot and concession and
city/town location. The database provides information regarding the location, type, size, land use, status and general comments.*
Government Publication Date: Sept 2002*
Aggregate Inventory: Provincial Arr-AGGR-bRb
This database of licensed and permitted pits and quarries is maintained by [COMPANY] ([CITY]), as regulated
under the Aggregate Resources Act, R.S.O. 1990. Aggregate site data has been divided into active and inactive sites. Active sites may be further
subdivided into partial surrenders. In partial surrenders, defined areas of a site are inactive while the rest of the site remains active.
Government Publication Date: Up to Nov 2023
[COMPANY]: Provincial Arr-MAMISI-Sbb
The Abandoned Mines Information System contains data on known abandoned and inactive mines located on both [COMPANY] and privately held lands. The
information was provided by [COMPANY] ([COMPANY]), with the following disclaimer: "the database provided has been
compiled from various sources, and [COMPANY] and Mines makes no representation and takes no responsibility that such
information is accurate, current or complete". Reported information includes official mine name, status, background information, mine start/end date,
primary commodity, mine features, hazards and remediation.
Government Publication Date: 1800-Mar 2022
[PERSON]'s Waste Disposal Sites: Private Arr-NANDDR-bRb
The information provided in this database was collected by examining various historical documents which aimed to characterize the likely position of
former waste disposal sites from 1860 to present. The research initiative behind the creation of this database was to identify those sites that are missing
from [COMPANY], as well as to provide revisions and corrections to the positions and descriptions of sites currently
listed in the [COMPANY] inventory. In addition to historic waste disposal facilities, the database also identifies certain auto wreckers and scrap yards that have
been extrapolated from documentary sources. Please note that the data is not warranted to be complete, exhaustive or authoritative. The information
was collected for research purposes only.
Government Publication Date: 1860s-Present
Aboveground Storage Tanks: Provincial Arr-ASST-Tbb
Historical listing of aboveground storage tanks made available by [COMPANY]. Includes tanks used to hold water
or petroleum. This dataset has been retired as of September 25, 2014 and will no longer be updated.
Government Publication Date: May 31, 2014
Automobile Wrecking & Supplies: Private Arr-UAUWWR-bbR
This database provides an inventory of known locations that are involved in the scrap metal, automobile wrecking/recycling, and automobile parts &
supplies industry. Information is provided on the company name, location and business type.
Government Publication Date: 1999-Oct 31, 2023
Borehole: Provincial Brr-OBORRE-bbE
A borehole is the generalized term for any narrow shaft drilled in the ground, either vertically or horizontally. The information here includes geotechnical
investigations or environmental site assessments, mineral exploration, or as a pilot hole for installing piers or underground utilities. Information is from
many sources such as [COMPANY] ([COMPANY]) boreholes from engineering reports and projects from the 1950 to 1990's in Southern
Ontario. Boreholes from [COMPANY] ([COMPANY]) including [COMPANY] (UGAIS) and the York Peel
Durham Toronto (YPDT) database of [COMPANY]. This database will include fields such as location, stratigraphy,
depth, elevation, year drilled, etc. For all water well data or oil and gas well data for Ontario please refer to [COMPANY] and [COMPANY].
Government Publication Date: 1875-Jul 2018
erisinfo.com | [COMPANY] Order No: 24041900105
Certificates of Approval: Provincial rrC-CAA-bb
This database contains the following types of approvals: [COMPANY], [COMPANY] and
Renewable Energy Approvals. The [COMPANY] in Ontario states that any facility that releases emissions to the atmosphere, discharges contaminants to
ground or surface water, provides potable water supplies, or stores, transports or disposes of waste, must have a Certificate of Approval before it can
operate lawfully. Fields include approval number, business name, address, approval date, approval type and status. This database will no longer be
updated, as CofA's have been replaced by either Environmental Activity and Sector Registry (EASR) or [COMPANY] ([COMPANY]).
Please refer to those individual databases for any information after Oct.31, 2011.
Government Publication Date: 1985-Oct 30, 2011*
[COMPANY]: Federal Crr-DCDRRY-bbY
List of dry cleaning facilities made available by Environment and Climate Change Canada. Environment and Climate Change Canada's
[PERSON] (Use in [COMPANY]) Regulations (SOR/2003-79) are intended to reduce releases of
tetrachloroethylene to the environment from dry cleaning facilities.
Government Publication Date: Jan 2004-Dec 2022
Commercial Fuel Oil Tanks: Provincial Crr-FCFOOT-bbT
Locations of commercial underground fuel oil tanks. This is not a comprehensive or complete inventory of commercial fuel tanks in the province; this
listing is a copy of records of registered commercial underground fuel oil tanks obtained under [COMPANY].
Note that the following types of tanks do not require registration: waste oil tanks in apartments, office buildings, residences, etc.; aboveground gas or
diesel tanks. Records are not verified for accuracy or completeness.
Government Publication Date: Oct 2023
Chemical Manufacturers and Distributors: Private Crr-HCHEEM-bMb
This database includes information from both a one time study conducted in 1992 and private source and is a listing of facilities that manufacture or
distribute chemicals. The production of these chemical substances may involve one or more chemical reactions and/or chemical separation processes
(i.e. fractionation, solvent extraction, crystallization, etc.).
Government Publication Date: 1999-Jan 31, 2020
[COMPANY]: Private Crr-CHHM-Mbb
This database includes a listing of locations of facilities within the [CITY] or Territory that either manufacture and/or distributes chemicals.
Government Publication Date: 1999-Oct 31, 2023
[COMPANY]: Private Crr-CNNG-Gbb
Canada has a network of public access compressed natural gas (CNG) refuelling stations. These stations dispense natural gas in compressed form at
3,000 pounds per square inch (psi), the pressure which is allowed within the current Canadian codes and standards. The majority of natural gas
refuelling is located at existing retail gasoline that have a separate refuelling island for natural gas. This list of stations is made available by the
[COMPANY].
Government Publication Date: Dec 2012 -Nov 2023
Inventory of Coal Gasification Plants and [COMPANY]

or Using Coal Tar and Related Tars in Ontario-November 1988) collected by the [COMPANY]. It identifies industrial sites that produced and continue to produce
or use coal tar and other related tars. Detailed information is available and includes: facility type, size, land use, information on adjoining properties, soil
condition, site operators/occupants, site description, potential environmental impacts and historic maps available. This was a one-time inventory.*

[PERSON]: Provincial Drr-DRRL-bLb
The Ontario Drill Hole Database contains information on more than 113,000 percussion, overburden, sonic and diamond drill holes from assessment
files on record with the department of [COMPANY]. Please note that limited data is available for southern Ontario, as it was the last area to be
completed. The database was created when surveys submitted to the Ministry were converted in [COMPANY]
([COMPANY]) project. However, the degree of accuracy (coordinates) as to the exact location of drill holes is dependent upon the source document submitted
to the [COMPANY]. Levels of accuracy used to locate holes are: centering on the mining claim; a sketch of the mining claim; a 1:50,000 map; a detailed
company map; or from submitted a "Report of Work".
Government Publication Date: 1886 - Aug 2023

regulatory agency under [COMPANY].

Environmental Activity and Sector Registry: Provincial Err-AEASSR-bRb
On October 31, 2011, a smarter, faster environmental approvals system came into effect in Ontario. The [COMPANY] allows businesses to register certain
activities with the ministry, rather than apply for an approval. The registry is available for common systems and processes, to which preset rules of
operation can be applied. The [COMPANY] is currently available for: heating systems, standby power systems and automotive refinishing. Businesses whose
activities aren't subject to the [COMPANY] may apply for an [COMPANY] (Environmental Compliance Approval), Please see our [COMPANY] database.
Government Publication Date: Oct 2011-Feb 29, 2024
Environmental Registry: Provincial Err-EBBR-Rbb
The Environmental Registry lists proposals, decisions and exceptions regarding policies, Acts, instruments, or regulations that could significantly affect
the environment. Through the [COMPANY], thirteen provincial ministries notify the public of upcoming proposals and invite their comments. For example, if a
local business is requesting a permit, license, or certificate of approval to release substances into the air or water; these are notified on the registry. Data
includes: Approval for discharge into the natural environment other than water (i.e. Air) - [COMPANY] s. 9, Approval for sewage works - OWRA s. 53(1), and
[COMPANY] s. 27 - Approval for a waste disposal site. For information regarding Permit to Take Water (PTTW), [COMPANY] Use ([COMPANY]) and ([COMPANY])
Orders please refer to those individual databases.

Environmental Compliance Approval: Provincial Err-ECCA-Abb
On October 31, 2011, a smarter, faster environmental approvals system came into effect in Ontario. In the past, a business had to apply for multiple
approvals (known as certificates of approval) for individual processes and pieces of equipment. Today, a business either registers itself, or applies for a
single approval, depending on the types of activities it conducts. Businesses whose activities aren't subject to the [COMPANY] may apply for an [COMPANY]. A single
[COMPANY] addresses all of a business's emissions, discharges and wastes. Separate approvals for air, noise and waste are no longer required. This database
will also include [COMPANY]. For certificates of approval prior to Nov 1st, 2011, please refer to the CA database. For all Waste
Disposal Sites please refer to the [COMPANY] database.

Ontario Regulation 347 Waste Generators Summary: Provincial Grr-GEEN-bNb
Regulation 347 of the Ontario [COMPANY] defines a waste generation site as any site, equipment and/or operation involved in the production, collection,
handling and/or storage of regulated wastes. A generator of regulated waste is required to register the waste generation site and each waste produced,
collected, handled, or stored at the site. This database contains the registration number, company name and address of registered generators including
the types of hazardous wastes generated. It includes data on waste generating facilities such as: drycleaners, waste treatment and disposal facilities,
machine shops, electric power distribution etc. This information is a summary of all years from 1986 including the most currently available data. Some
records may contain, within the company name, the phrase "See & Use..." followed by a series of letters and numbers. This occurs when one company
is amalgamated with or taken over by another registered company. The number listed as "See & Use", refers to the new ownership and the other
identification number refers to the original ownership. This phrase serves as a link between the 2 companies until operations have been fully
transferred.

Mineral Occurrences: Provincial Mrr-MNNR-bRb
In the early 70's, [COMPANY] and Mines created an inventory of approximately 19,000 mineral occurrences in Ontario, in
regard to metallic and industrial minerals, as well as some information on building stones and aggregate deposits. Please note that [COMPANY] Accuracy" is approximately +/- 200 m. Many reference elements for each record were derived from field sketches using pace or chain/tape
measurements against claim posts or topographic features in the area. The primary limiting factor for the level of positional accuracy is the scale of the
source material. The testing of horizontal accuracy of the source materials was accomplished by comparing the plan metric (X and Y) coordinates of that
point with the coordinates of the same point as defined from a source of higher accuracy.

This database describes locations and characteristics of water wells found within Ontario in accordance with Regulation 903. It includes such
information as coordinates, construction date, well depth, primary and secondary use, pump rate, static water level, well status, etc. Also included are
detailed stratigraphy information, approximate depth to bedrock and the approximate depth to the water table.
Government Publication Date: Mar 31 2023

approximation.
